				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>

It is not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Conservative%E2%80%93Liberal_Democrat_coalition_agreement" title="Conservative–Liberal Democrat coalition agreement">Conservative–Liberal Democrat coalition agreement</a>.</div>

<p><a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron&#39;s signature"><img alt="David Cameron&#39;s signature" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Accession_Treaty_2011_David_Cameron_signature.svg/150px-Accession_Treaty_2011_David_Cameron_signature.svg.png" width="150" height="55" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Accession_Treaty_2011_David_Cameron_signature.svg/225px-Accession_Treaty_2011_David_Cameron_signature.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Accession_Treaty_2011_David_Cameron_signature.svg/300px-Accession_Treaty_2011_David_Cameron_signature.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="337" data-file-height="123" /></a><br />
</p>
<a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom"><img alt="Government of the United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28HM_Government%29.svg/60px-Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28HM_Government%29.svg.png" width="60" height="49" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28HM_Government%29.svg/90px-Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28HM_Government%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28HM_Government%29.svg/120px-Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%28HM_Government%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1530" data-file-height="1256" /></a></td>
</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;text-align:center;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:David_Cameron_sidebar" title="Template:David Cameron sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:David_Cameron_sidebar" title="Template talk:David Cameron sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:David_Cameron_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nick_Clegg" title="Nick Clegg">Nick Clegg</a> formed the <b>Cameron–Clegg coalition</b><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> after the former was invited by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> to begin a new government, following the resignation of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a> on 11 May 2010. It was the first <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition government</a> in the UK since the <a href="/wiki/Churchill_war_ministry" title="Churchill war ministry">Churchill war ministry</a> and was led by Cameron with Clegg as <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Deputy Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Deputy</a>, composed of members of both the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">Cabinet</a> was made up of sixteen Conservatives and five Liberal Democrats, with eight other Conservatives and one other Liberal Democrat attending cabinet but not members.<sup id="cite_ref-coalition_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coalition-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The coalition was replaced by the single-party <a href="/wiki/Second_Cameron_ministry" title="Second Cameron ministry">Cameron ministry</a> after the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_government_formation" title="2010 United Kingdom government formation">2010 United Kingdom government formation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Premiership_of_David_Cameron" title="Premiership of David Cameron">Premiership of David Cameron</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Lib%E2%80%93Con_pact" title="Lib–Con pact">Lib–Con pact</a></div>
<p>The previous Parliament had been dissolved on 12 April 2010 in advance of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">general election on 6 May</a>. The election resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Hung_parliament" title="Hung parliament">hung parliament</a>, no single party having an overall majority in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>, the Conservatives having the most seats but 20 short of a majority.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Conservative%E2%80%93Liberal_Democrat_coalition_agreement" title="Conservative–Liberal Democrat coalition agreement">Conservative–Liberal Democrat coalition agreement</a> of 11 May 2010, the two parties formed a coalition government.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The new Parliament met on 18 May for the swearing-in of Peers in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> and newly elected and returning Members of Parliament in the House of Commons, and the election for the Speakership of the House of Commons. The <a href="/wiki/Speech_from_the_throne" title="Speech from the throne">Queen's Speech</a> on 25 May set out the government's legislative agenda. Of the 57 Liberal Democrat MPs, only two refused to support the Conservative Coalition agreement, with former leader <a href="/wiki/Charles_Kennedy" title="Charles Kennedy">Charles Kennedy</a> and Manchester Withington MP <a href="/wiki/John_Leech_(politician)" title="John Leech (politician)">John Leech</a> both rebelling.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Liberal Democrats had five Cabinet members including <a href="/wiki/Nick_Clegg" title="Nick Clegg">Nick Clegg</a> as <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Deputy Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Deputy Prime Minister</a> though after the Cabinet and ministerial <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_reshuffle" title="Cabinet reshuffle">reshuffle</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Laws" title="David Laws">David Laws</a>, who was a <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State" title="Minister of State">Minister of State</a>, was allowed to attend the Cabinet but was not a full member. If a Liberal Democrat minister resigned or was removed from office, another member of the same party would have had to be appointed to the Cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-qanda_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qanda-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_cabinet_committee" title="United Kingdom cabinet committee">cabinet committee</a> had a chair from one party and a deputy chair from the other; there was also a cabinet committee specifically overseeing the operation of the coalition. Both parties' ministers shared <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_collective_responsibility" title="Cabinet collective responsibility">collective responsibility</a> for the government's positions, although the coalition agreement detailed several issues on which the parties agreed to differ; the Liberal Democrats abstained from voting in such cases. Clegg, as Deputy Prime Minister, took <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister%27s_Questions" title="Prime Minister&#39;s Questions">Prime Minister's Questions</a> (PMQ) when Cameron was unavailable.<sup id="cite_ref-qanda_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qanda-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While the <a href="/wiki/British_Government_frontbench" title="British Government frontbench">government's front benchers</a> sat together in the House of Commons and the two parties acted as a bloc during PMQ,<sup id="cite_ref-riddell20100519_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riddell20100519-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> the Liberal Democrat and Conservative <a href="/wiki/Backbencher" title="Backbencher">backbenchers</a> sat apart and each had their own <a href="/wiki/Chief_Whip#United_Kingdom" title="Chief Whip">whips</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-riddell20100519_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riddell20100519-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and the two parties competed in <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Kingdom_by-elections_(2010%E2%80%93present)" title="List of United Kingdom by-elections (2010–present)">by-elections</a>. On 4 September 2012, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> <a href="/wiki/2012_British_cabinet_reshuffle" title="2012 British cabinet reshuffle">reshuffled his cabinet</a> for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He <a href="/wiki/2014_British_cabinet_reshuffle" title="2014 British cabinet reshuffle">reshuffled his cabinet</a> for the second time on 14 July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCres_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCres-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 August 2013, the Conservative-led coalition <a href="/wiki/List_of_Government_defeats_in_the_House_of_Commons_(1945%E2%80%93present)#Cameron_(coalition_government)" title="List of Government defeats in the House of Commons (1945–present)">suffered a defeat</a> when Parliament voted against UK military attacks on Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-blow_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blow-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabinets">Cabinets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cabinets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Changes">Changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/David_Laws" title="David Laws">David Laws</a> resigned as Chief Secretary to the Treasury on 29 May 2010 because of an <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_parliamentary_expenses_scandal" title="United Kingdom parliamentary expenses scandal">expenses irregularity</a> dating from the previous Parliament. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Danny_Alexander" title="Danny Alexander">Danny Alexander</a>, who was in turn replaced as Secretary of State for Scotland by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Moore_(Scottish_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Moore (Scottish politician)">Michael Moore</a><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On 14 October 2011 <a href="/wiki/Liam_Fox" title="Liam Fox">Liam Fox</a> resigned as Secretary of State for Defence following the procurement of high-level overseas meetings attendance for his friend and advisor, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Werrity" class="mw-redirect" title="Adam Werrity">Adam Werrity</a>, working for a private contractor, and stated that he had "mistakenly allowed the distinction between my personal interest and my government activities to become blurred"<sup id="cite_ref-Fox1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox1-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> His successor was <a href="/wiki/Philip_Hammond" title="Philip Hammond">Philip Hammond</a> who was replaced as Transport Secretary by <a href="/wiki/Justine_Greening" title="Justine Greening">Justine Greening</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Secretary_to_the_Treasury" title="Economic Secretary to the Treasury">Economic Secretary to the Treasury</a>, who was in turn replaced by <a href="/wiki/Chloe_Smith" title="Chloe Smith">Chloe Smith</a>, an assistant government whip: she was replaced in turn by <a href="/wiki/Greg_Hands" title="Greg Hands">Greg Hands</a><sup id="cite_ref-Fox1_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox1-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On 3 February 2012 <a href="/wiki/Chris_Huhne" title="Chris Huhne">Chris Huhne</a> resigned as Secretary of State for Energy and Climate Change following the decision of the Crown Prosecution Service to <a href="/wiki/R_v_Huhne" title="R v Huhne">prosecute him and his former wife</a>. His successor was <a href="/wiki/Ed_Davey" title="Ed Davey">Edward Davey</a>, who was replaced as a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Under-Secretary_of_State" title="Parliamentary Under-Secretary of State">Parliamentary Under-Secretary of State</a> in the Department of Business, Innovation and Skills by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Lamb" title="Norman Lamb">Norman Lamb</a>, replaced in his previous dual roles by <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Willott" title="Jenny Willott">Jenny Willott</a> as an Assistant Whip and <a href="/wiki/Jo_Swinson" title="Jo Swinson">Jo Swinson</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Private_Secretary" title="Parliamentary Private Secretary">Parliamentary Private Secretary</a> to the Deputy Prime Minister<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span id="September_2012_.E2.80.93_July_2014"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="September_2012_–_July_2014">September 2012 – July 2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: September 2012 – July 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_2">Changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>On 19 October 2012, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Mitchell" title="Andrew Mitchell">Andrew Mitchell</a> resigned as Government Chief Whip in the House of Commons following <a href="/wiki/Plebgate" title="Plebgate">controversy surrounding an argument with police officers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Downing_Street" title="Downing Street">Downing Street</a>. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Sir_George_Young" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir George Young">Sir George Young</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mitchell1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mitchell1-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On 7 January 2013, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Galbraith,_2nd_Baron_Strathclyde" title="Thomas Galbraith, 2nd Baron Strathclyde">Lord Strathclyde</a> resigned as Leader of the House of Lords and Chancellor of the Duchy of Lancaster. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Hill,_Baron_Hill_of_Oareford" title="Jonathan Hill, Baron Hill of Oareford">Lord Hill of Oareford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On 7 October 2013, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Moore_(Scottish_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Moore (Scottish politician)">Michael Moore</a> was replaced as Secretary of State for Scotland by <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Carmichael" title="Alistair Carmichael">Alistair Carmichael</a>, during a reshuffle which focused on junior ministerial ranks.</li>
<li>On 9 April 2014, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Miller" title="Maria Miller">Maria Miller</a> resigned as Secretary of State for Culture, Media and Sport and Minister for Women and Equalities. She was replaced as Culture Secretary and Minister for Equalities by <a href="/wiki/Sajid_Javid" title="Sajid Javid">Sajid Javid</a>, and by <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Morgan" title="Nicky Morgan">Nicky Morgan</a> as Minister for Women. Morgan, who succeeded Javid as <a href="/wiki/Financial_Secretary_to_the_Treasury" title="Financial Secretary to the Treasury">Financial Secretary to the Treasury</a>, was not a full cabinet member but attended meetings in her role as Minister for Women.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span id="July_2014_.E2.80.93_May_2015"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="July_2014_–_May_2015">July 2014 – May 2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: July 2014 – May 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_3">Changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>On 5 August 2014, <a href="/wiki/Sayeeda_Warsi,_Baroness_Warsi" title="Sayeeda Warsi, Baroness Warsi">Baroness Warsi</a> resigned as Minister of State at the Foreign and Commonwealth Office, and as Minister for Faith and Community, in protest at the Government's response to the <a href="/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2014 Israel–Gaza conflict">conflict in the Gaza Strip</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> She was replaced at the Foreign Office by <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Anelay,_Baroness_Anelay_of_St_John%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Joyce Anelay, Baroness Anelay of St John&#39;s">Baroness Anelay of St. Johns</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Communities_and_Local_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for Communities and Local Government">Communities and Local Government Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Eric_Pickles" title="Eric Pickles">Eric Pickles</a> taking on Warsi's former Faith and Community brief.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_ministers">List of ministers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: List of ministers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
